1936.02.28

Mobilization of Japanese Army and Navy for Security Cabinet Resigns, Tokyo Under Martial Law Takahashi Dies of Severe Injuries, Saionji Escapes Due to Early Warning Mutinying Soldiers, Approximately 1,000, Agree to Return to Barracks This Morning After Negotiations Reasons for the Revolt Still Being Investigated, Diminishing the Emperor Organ Theory 1

Tokyo. Following Prime Minister Okada's assassination by mutinous soldiers yesterday, Goto, who was appointed acting prime minister, submitted the cabinet's resignation this morning. As Goto remains the Home Minister, the overall situation here remains unchanged. The Emperor issued an edict at night, declaring martial law in Tokyo. The mutinous soldiers, who occupied government offices and cabinet members' residences since dawn yesterday, have not yet been driven out. These rebels, totaling 2,400, belong to the Third Regiment of the First Division, which was ordered to Manchuria. According to the Ministry of Home Affairs, Japan's entire public order is now maintained by the military in agreement with the police, so there is no cause for concern. It is reported that Lieutenant General Hori, commander of the First Division, advocated taking severe action against the mutinous soldiers. However, some believe it should be resolved through negotiations. There is no doubt that the mutinous soldiers have the support of influential military personnel. The cabinet, after lengthy consideration, finally decided to implement martial law. This measure was approved by the Emperor at 2:30 AM. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the Tokyo Garrison Commander first announced a state of emergency. At dawn yesterday, a group of young officers, all tearing off their shoulder patches to avoid recognition, braved the heavy snow and traveled by car to the private residence of Watanabe, the Inspector General of Military Education, and began their attack. Watanabe was killed on the spot. A newspaper delivery boy witnessed everything and immediately informed his newspaper by telephone, which is how the newspaper obtained the news. Another group of young officers stormed the private residence of Prime Minister Okada. Okada was awakened from his sleep. The rebels saw him and immediately shot him in the head, killing him. The rebels then occupied his residence and made it their headquarters. The private residences of Saito, Takahashi, and Suzuki were also attacked by soldiers in heavy vehicles.

The renowned elder statesman, Duke Saionji, resides in the countryside near Tokyo. He apparently received an early warning and took refuge in the residence of the prefectural governor. Therefore, the rebels failed to find and harm him when they arrived at his residence. Count Makino resides near a coastal resort sixty miles from Tokyo and was attacked by ten mutinous soldiers. One of his guards bravely resisted the rebels for some time, seriously wounding an officer before being knocked down. The rebels then rushed into the house. The Countess Makino stepped forward and told them that her husband had gone out. At that moment, the Count suddenly escaped through the back door and took refuge in the home of a carpenter he knew nearby.

People here now mostly believe that this rebellion is not unfavorable to the Emperor. Moreover, the young officers who masterminded this rebellion are all "supreme loyalists." Their actions are driven by a desire to restore and strengthen the Emperor's prerogatives and to eradicate the "Emperor Organ" theory. They accuse the Okada cabinet of weakness in governance, which encouraged certain cliques to usurp the Emperor's authority, and of weakness in its foreign policy toward Russia and China, hence their deep hatred. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. The Ministry of Finance announced on the 27th that Finance Minister Takahashi passed away on the same day, the 26th, due to severe injuries from an unforeseen disaster. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. According to sources responsible tonight, the mutinous soldiers who launched a violent coup yesterday, assassinating four major politicians and occupying several government offices, have agreed to return to their barracks peacefully at 8:00 AM tomorrow. After the authorities negotiated with the mutinous soldiers this afternoon to avoid further bloodshed and end the coup, the mutinous soldiers made this decision. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. At 8:00 PM tonight, three leaders of the mutinous soldiers were summoned to the Army Club by three military councilors, including General Masaki, who told them that the incident must be resolved immediately, or they would be dealt with by force. The three then returned to their headquarters in Prime Minister Okada's residence. An hour later, they met with General Masaki and others at the headquarters of the Military Police and said they would accept the suggestion to return to their barracks. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. Large numbers of troops entered the city at night. From the morning, soldiers with bayonets mounted on their rifles guarded the entrances of all government offices not occupied by the mutinous soldiers. The overall situation was peaceful throughout the night, but the weather was very cold and snowy, which dampened the mutinous soldiers' spirit. It is reported that the mutinous soldiers now "regret" their actions, so it is expected that they will be allowed to return to their barracks peacefully today. It is now known that the mutinous soldiers number only one thousand. The earlier report of three thousand was a misreport in the confusion. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Washington. According to reliable sources here today, Japanese officers distributed pamphlets to major Japanese newspapers stating that this coup was caused by the government infringing upon the Emperor's prerogatives. They said that government officials had "lost the true spirit of Japan" and that if these policies were not changed, Japan's relations with China, Russia, Britain, and the United States would inevitably break down. (National News Agency dispatch, 26th)

Tokyo. Although the entire city of Tokyo remains as peaceful as usual, the political situation is still precarious. Warships ordered to Tokyo and Osaka have now arrived at their destinations, but many warships remain in Yokosuka, awaiting possible deployment. Troops from various regions are also rushing to the capital. (National News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Important Army Conference 2

Tokyo. The Army Military Councilors held a meeting at the Kaiko-sha at 10:30 AM on the 27th. Princes Asaka and Nashimoto, as well as Councilors Hayashi, Masaki, Araki, Abe, Ueda, Terauchi, Nishi, and Sugiyama, all attended. They discussed important issues and reached an agreement.

After the Army Military Councilors met at the Kaiko-sha, they went to the Imperial Palace to meet with cabinet members and report the results of their discussions. At 9:00 AM, they went to the Army Hall to meet with the heads of the Army Ministry and the General Staff Headquarters to report the same matters and seek their agreement. The current incident is therefore expected to be resolved.

As a result of the Army Military Councilors' meeting last night, the top leadership of the army decided on a policy for the current incident. General Ueda, as their representative, left Tokyo at 2:00 PM this afternoon for Odawara to meet with Chief of the General Staff, Prince Kan'in, to report everything and request his decision. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

The Emperor Dispatches an Envoy to Visit Saionji to Consult on the Appointment of a New Cabinet Meeting of Senior Statesmen Cannot Be Reconvened Frenzy Over the Selection of a New Prime Minister 3

Tokyo. It is reported that the Emperor has dispatched an imperial envoy to Elder Statesman Saionji to consult on the formation of a successor cabinet. According to past practice, Prince Saionji would immediately come to Tokyo to hear the opinions of senior statesmen and observe the political situation. However, the senior statesmen Saito, Takahashi, Okada, and Suzuki are either dead or injured and cannot convene a meeting of senior statesmen. It is therefore noteworthy what method Prince Saionji will use to decide on the selection of a successor cabinet. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. Meetings were held today at the Imperial Palace and other places to discuss the overall situation and the formation of a new government. Other politicians, such as Count Kiyoura and Baron Ichiki, also attended the palace meeting. The Military Council held a meeting last night and continued its deliberations this morning. Those currently hoping to be appointed as the new Prime Minister include Prince Konoe, President of the House of Peers; General Araki, Military Councilor; General Masaki; Admiral Yamamoto; Baron Hiranuma, President of the Privy Council; General Ugaki, Governor-General of Korea; and General Minami, Commander of the Kwantung Army. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. Prince Konoe, President of the House of Peers, is hoping to be appointed as the new Prime Minister. The Prince is 45 years old and accompanied Prince Saionji to Europe in 1918 to participate in the peace conference. (Reuters dispatch, 27th) Gyeongseong. Governor-General of Korea, Ugaki Kazunari, who had been resting at the Kaiundai Hot Springs, suddenly returned to Gyeongseong at 3:00 PM on the 27th. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. Prince Chichibu, the Emperor's brother, who is stationed in Hirosaki with his regiment, has been ordered to return to Tokyo. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

The Cabinet Temporarily Remains in the Imperial Palace 4

Tokyo. The cabinet decided to resign en masse late on the 26th. Acting Prime Minister Goto collected the letters of resignation from each cabinet member and presented them to the Emperor. However, upon the Emperor's edict, they will temporarily administer state affairs until a successor cabinet is formed. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. Commerce Minister Machida, due to the difficulties of the Finance Minister, has decided to concurrently assume the position of Finance Minister. At 9:00 AM on the 27th, the appointment ceremony was held in the presence of Acting Prime Minister Goto. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Tokyo. Cabinet members gathered in the Imperial Palace to discuss the aftermath. Before the formation of a successor cabinet, they will not leave the Imperial Palace, except for special matters, to await the stabilization of the situation. They will also remain in the Imperial Palace on the evening of the 27th. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

The Financial World Temporarily Observes Quietly 5

Tokyo. Finance Officer Tsushima met with the President of the Bank of Japan, Fukai, and the President of the Yokohama Specie Bank, Kodama, at Finance Minister Takahashi's private residence on the evening of the 26th. After listening to the situation in the financial world, they discussed countermeasures. However, as the business conditions of central and local banks have not shown any signs of wavering, it has been decided to temporarily observe the situation in the financial world quietly.

Tokyo. Finance Officer Tsushima said that there were no changes in the financial world on the morning of the 27th. If something should happen, the Ministry of Finance has measures in place to deal with it.

The head offices and branches of the Bank of Japan and Mitsui, Mitsubishi, Dai-Ichi, Yasuda, Kawasaki, Dai-Hyaku, Kangyo, Kogyo, and other banks are operating as usual on the 27th.

Tokyo. The Rice Exchange decided to suspend trading today. The Tokyo and Osaka Stock Exchanges have also suspended trading. The Osaka Sanpin Exchange, the Sugar Exchange, and the Clearing House are operating as usual.

Tokyo. The Exchange held a meeting at 11:00 AM on the 27th to discuss the aftermath. As a result, it was decided to continue the suspension of trading for the 28th and 29th.

Kobe. The Kobe Exchange held an emergency meeting of its Securities, Rice, and other divisions on the morning of the 27th. As a result, it was decided to suspend trading on the 27th.

Yokohama. The Yokohama Exchange decided to temporarily close on the 27th. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

State of Martial Law in Tokyo 6

Tokyo. The government issued an extra edition of the official gazette on the 27th. The contents are as follows: "We, recognizing the urgent necessity, and after consulting with the Privy Council, in accordance with Article 8, Paragraph 1 of the Japanese Constitution, approve the application of the necessary provisions of the Martial Law Ordinance within a certain area. We hereby announce this."

Order of the Martial Law Headquarters Commander: Article 1. The Martial Law Headquarters Commander will be appointed by the Emperor from the ranks of Army General or Lieutenant General. He will report directly to the Emperor and be responsible for the security of Tokyo City. The Commander will direct the army within the aforementioned area to accomplish the task. This order will take effect from the date of its promulgation. The duties of the Tokyo Garrison Commander within Tokyo City are temporarily suspended.

Lieutenant General Kashii, Commander of the Martial Law Headquarters, issued the following proclamation at 8:00 AM on the 27th. The purpose of enforcing some provisions of the Martial Law Ordinance in Tokyo City, as stated in the previous proclamation, is to maintain the overall public order in the vicinity of the capital, protect important objects, and at the same time, pre-empt the reckless actions of rioters. I am now entrusted with the great task of using military force to provide security in the martial law area, administer judicial and administrative affairs, and judicial affairs related to military affairs. I hope that officials and civilians in the martial law area can understand this principle, cooperate and be prudent in their words and actions, and trust me, so that the implementation of martial law can be carried out without regret. After the major incident that occurred in Tokyo City yesterday, the public was greatly shaken for a time. However, after the promulgation of the Martial Law Ordinance at 3:00 AM on the 27th, public order was established and the public's sentiment gradually calmed down. The Martial Law Headquarters is located at the Kudan Military Hall. Along the road from there to the Takebashi Gate, a military policeman stands every three feet, holding a bayoneted rifle, maintaining strict vigilance. The gates of the Imperial Palace are all guarded by soldiers in yellow uniforms, armed for security. The atmosphere around the Prime Minister's residence, the Army Ministry, and the General Staff Headquarters is tense. However, the bustling areas of Ginza and Showa Street are no different from usual. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Current Commentary

The Issue of Interest Rate Reduction in the Financial Industry 8

— Liu

The issue of interest rate reduction, which the industrial and commercial sectors have long desired, has been widely discussed. Recently, foreign banks have already implemented interest rate reductions on deposits. As for Chinese banks, although they have taken measures to accept bills of exchange for discounting, their standards are limited to warehouse receipts for domestic goods stored in bank warehouses. This assistance to domestic industries is undoubtedly beneficial. However, the issue of interest rate reduction has not yet been concretely resolved, and general industrial and commercial enterprises still feel that their operating income is only enough to cover the interest on loans.

The difficulty in resolving the issue of interest rate reduction is not simply a matter of bargaining chips. The source of funds is the ability to produce. Regarding China's production, agriculture still has not escaped the small-peasant system. Although handicrafts are declining, new enterprises are difficult to develop due to foreign economic aggression. As there is no prospect of increasing wealth, people who have a little property have all accumulated it through small savings. Since it is difficult to obtain, they value it highly. Depositing it for interest to seek high profits is a natural trend. In this regard, the law cannot impose strict restrictions. According to the provisions of the Civil Code regarding payable interest, if the interest rate has not been specified or there is no legal basis, the annual interest rate is 5%. If the agreed interest rate exceeds 12% per annum, the debtor may repay the principal at any time after one year. If the agreed interest rate exceeds 20% per annum, the creditor has no right to claim interest exceeding that amount (Civil Code, Articles 203-5). It can be seen that 20% is the highest interest rate, but if the debtor is willing to pay an interest rate of more than 20%, the law does not expressly prohibit it. This is with regard to cash. As for real estate, according to the provisions of the Land Law and the standards for house rents, it is limited to no more than 12% of the annual interest on the land and buildings as recorded in the land price register (Land Law, Article 163). The administrative measures for mediating rental disputes recently formulated by the Executive Yuan also have the same provisions (see Article 2 of the measures). If the statutory interest rate is like this, and the investment trend of the financial industry in recent years has been mostly in securities, the level of interest will always fluctuate with the arbitrage profits of the securities. The weekly interest rates of the two unified reconstruction bonds recently issued are both 6%. It is difficult to predict how the market price will be in the future. If the combined interest rate is very high, it will be an obstacle to the prospect of interest rate reduction.

Recently, Mr. Sheng Kezhong investigated the general situation of interest rates in Shanghai banks. According to his statistics, the highest standard interest rates are 6-7% for ordinary deposits, and 6-9% for savings deposits. Lending interest rates are divided into two types, with monthly interest rates of 5-8% (see this newspaper's 164th issue of the Economic Special). Although this cannot be regarded as conclusive, the future trend of interest rate reduction should ultimately be weighed between the current interest rates and market conditions. I believe that the level of interest is still a trivial matter. In the past, in the days when the silver and money industry was undeveloped and the rural economy was well-off, those with wealth, in addition to burying it, either operated it themselves to generate profits or deposited it in stores to earn interest. In recent years, large-scale enterprises have flourished, raising capital and absorbing deposits. At first, the general public was enthusiastic about investing, but often they did not achieve good results, which led them to regard it with fear. If they can earnestly improve from the production business, manage it properly, and establish good credit, why worry about the difficulty of circulating funds, and why bother about demanding interest rate reductions from the financial industry?

Tokyo Military Uprising: American Sighs, British Anxiety; Soviet Authorities Fear Border Crisis Escalation; Germans Say Such a Mutiny Could Not Happen in Berlin 13

London

The Tokyo coup has caused anxiety worldwide. Members of Parliament today repeatedly questioned Foreign Secretary Eden. The anxiety of British officials is evident here. Eden, in response to Labor MP Attlee's question about the situation in Japan, said that both Prime Minister Okada and former Prime Minister Saito had been killed. Eden replied that, as far as he knew at present, the coup had not endangered British interests. Paris also showed a panic-stricken atmosphere after hearing about the Tokyo coup. Stock market prices plummeted, and newspapers even said that this matter would endanger peace in the Far East, and that besides China and Russia, it might involve other countries. An editorial in the Paris Communications newspaper stated that Japanese militarists have always been hostile to Europeans, and European events have also served to encourage them. A Reuters dispatch from Moscow stated that Russian opinion believes that if Japanese military personnel seize power, the result will either be the resumption of aggression in the Far East or internal strife among Japanese parties. All newspapers are carrying the news on their front pages. The German Daily News stated that the Soviet Union's rearmament has almost prompted the motive for this coup. The Berlin Daily News stated that the matter is partly due to the domestic political situation and partly due to the imperialist trend towards Russia. The National Socialist Party newspaper believes that the tension between the military and politicians is the main cause of this coup. (Reuters, 27th)

London Many circles in Britain are panicked by the coup in Tokyo, believing it to be a prelude to large-scale military operations in the Far East. Will the government of Japan or a small number of irresponsible, rash young officers control national policy in the future? This is also a question. The Daily Telegraph stated that this kind of cruel and inexcusable militarism is a danger to domestic peace in Japan and tranquility in the Far East. The Japanese are a nation loyal to their emperor, patriotic, strong, and fond of war, and their minds have been nurtured by imperialism. Now their army leaders are displaying extremely arrogant claims, which will inevitably have major consequences. The Manchester Guardian stated that the extreme faction of the Japanese army has now become intensely nationalistic. Compared to German National Socialism, National Socialism is like a faint candlelight. If the Tokyo soldiers succeed, the future will indeed be dark. But even if the government and the moderate faction in the army gain control, the military will feel that their influence has been strengthened by this coup. The deaths of Okada, Watanabe, and Saito are a loss to the bureaucratic faction. With Takahashi already gone, even the moderate faction of the army will not be able to resist the demand for increased military spending, let alone civilians. The best hope today lies only in the continuation of the bureaucratic government, supported by the moderate faction of the army, but not dominated by it. (Reuters, 27th)

Washington The government is clearly paying close attention to developments in Japan, but does not want to criticize them until the situation unfolds. Public Telegram

The Guoyang County Drought Relief Association Appeals for Spring Relief

To the Shanghai Shen Bao Newspaper and all agencies, charitable organizations, great philanthropists, newspapers, and the fathers, elders, brothers, sisters, aunts, and sisters throughout the country: We, in Guoyang, have suffered frequent disasters in recent years, but none have been as widespread or affected as many people as today. Although the Shanghai Drought Relief Association for the Provinces has allocated 6,000 yuan for emergency relief, as well as clothing and medicine, it is like a drop in the bucket, and can only save a limited number of people. Now that spring has just begun and the autumn harvest is still far away, we are urgently requesting officials to handle spring relief so that the disaster victims can prolong their lives and have resources for cultivation, in order to have hope for a harvest. In addition to requesting relief agencies to provide relief, and widely soliciting relief opinions from this association, we are specially publishing this notice to solicit relief. We beseech benevolent gentlemen to have compassion for those who are hungry and drowning, and to have great compassion and great mercy. Donating wheat is always a good deed, and donating money is always helpful, no matter how little. If you are willing to contribute generously, no matter the amount, this association will collect and distribute it immediately, benefiting the disaster victims. We urgently appeal and respectfully hope for your kind consideration, looking forward from afar with gratitude. Sincerely, Wang Jiju, Chairman of the Guoyang County Drought Disaster Relief Committee, Standing Committee members Ge Lianyuan, Liu Furen, Wang Jianhua, Liu Xianggu, Zhang Shanfu, Liu Yunzhi, Wang Huixuan, Wang Zhemin, collectively bowing in respect.

League of Nations to Convene Meeting to Discuss Intensified Sanctions Against Italy Britain Authorizes Eden to Act Expediently Sweden to Propose New Suggestions to Revive the Declining Situation

Paris

The League of Nations' Eighteen-Nation Committee is scheduled to meet on the second of next month to discuss intensifying sanctions against Italy. French Foreign Minister Flandin and British Foreign Secretary Eden will both attend the meeting in Geneva. According to a Times reporter stationed in Geneva, the two are believed to be discussing the following issue: What kind of situation will arise if Germany violates the demilitarized zone along the Rhine River? (26th Havas dispatch)

London

According to members of Parliament who advocate sanctions, if the ban on oil cannot be implemented when the League of Nations Eighteen-Nation Committee meets on the second of next month, the Swedish representative will propose new measures to intensify sanctions, intending to include coal, iron ore, and pig iron in the list of banned items. At the same time, it is also suggested that the ports belonging to countries participating in the sanctions should not allow Italian ships to dock. (26th Havas dispatch)

London

The Cabinet held a meeting this morning to discuss intensifying sanctions against Italy. According to inquiries, the attending cabinet members unanimously agreed to authorize Foreign Secretary Eden to act expediently when attending the League of Nations Eighteen-Nation Committee on the second of next month to discuss the ban on oil, adopting the opinions of the majority of the committee members to determine Britain's position. It is heard that the Cabinet believes that since the United States is currently outside the matter, it is difficult to expect results even if the oil ban is implemented at this moment. However, for the sake of the League of Nations' prestige, it is regrettable if the pressure of sanctions is not intensified. It is generally believed that when the Eighteen-Nation Committee meets, if no other country agrees to Sweden's proposal to revive the declining situation, the result of the committee's discussion on the oil ban will be delayed until the environment is suitable for further discussion. (26th Havas dispatch)

British-Russian Loan Negotiations Enter Active Stage

London

Regarding the issue of the Soviet Union borrowing money from Britain, negotiations between the two countries have been going on for a long time. At the beginning of this month, the British Cabinet sent personnel to Moscow to work with the Soviet authorities to formulate the detailed rules of the loan and the collateral that the Soviet Union could provide. According to financial sources, the negotiation situation in Moscow has entered an active stage, and the British government has now sent a formal representative to continue consultations. The total amount of this loan is 40 million pounds, with a term of 20 years and an annual interest rate of up to 6%. The British government will also issue domestic bonds of the same amount with an annual interest rate of 2% to meet this loan. The difference in interest rates of 4% will be used to settle the debt owed to Britain during the Tsarist era. (26th Havas dispatch)

Italy Expresses Opposition to Tonnage Figures to the United States A Smokescreen English Presents Draft Agreement to Germany Fate of Naval Conference May Be Determined in Geneva

London

The head of the Italian delegation to the naval conference, Grandi, met with the head of the American delegation, Davis, at 5:00 PM today. According to our reporter, Grandi explained to Davis that Italy firmly opposes the figures of 35,000 tons for battleships and 10,000 tons for Class A cruisers. It is generally believed that Italy's technical objection is actually a smokescreen, intended to conceal its political opposition. The American side is very pessimistic about this, believing that Italy's opposition will not diminish before the League of Nations Eighteen-Nation Committee meets. (26th Havas dispatch)

London

The Italian Ambassador to Britain, Grandi, plans to visit the British Foreign Office to study the political issues that will be caused by the technical problems within the agenda of the naval conference. German Ambassador Dr. Hoesch and Naval Counselor visited the British Foreign Office this afternoon and were received by the Foreign Secretary and the Secretary of the Navy. It is heard that they discussed how Germany could join any treaty resulting from the naval conference. (26th Reuters dispatch)

London

German Ambassador Dr. Hoesch led Embassy Counselor Bismarck and Naval Counselor Colonel Hüssner to the Foreign Office this afternoon to talk with Foreign Secretary Eden and Naval Minister Lord Monsell. Eden presented Hoesch with a draft naval agreement, which Hoesch then sent to Berlin for review. The contents of this case specify the qualitative restrictions that have been agreed upon by Britain, France, the United States, and Italy, and also include the figures of 35,000 tons for battleships and 10,000 tons for Class A cruisers, which have not yet been unanimously accepted by all countries. Eden is scheduled to present this draft to Italian Ambassador Grandi tomorrow to inquire whether he can accept it. (26th Havas dispatch)

London

American sources here believe that if the talks between Britain and Italy do not yield results, the naval conference cannot continue for long and will inevitably be adjourned in a short time. If so, Britain may directly conclude naval treaties with countries willing to sign them and then wait for other countries to sign and participate. In any case, the fate of the naval conference will be determined within a few days. (26th Havas dispatch)

Tensions Rise Between Germany and Switzerland

London

After the leader of the Swiss National Socialist Party group, Gustloff (a German national), was assassinated in Switzerland, the Swiss Federal Government ordered the prohibition of the establishment of National Socialist Party organs within the country. Subsequently, the German government protested to Switzerland. The Manchester Guardian commented on this matter: "Relations between Switzerland and Germany" have become tense as a result. It is expected that when the Swiss government responds to Germany's protest, it will inevitably insist on its original proposal to ban the establishment of National Socialist Party organs, without a doubt. The current situation is becoming more serious, for two reasons:

1. Germany is building fortifications near the Swiss border.

2. The concentration point of German troops in that area is the city of Donaueschingen, and German troops are constantly being transferred there. Therefore, the Swiss authorities are also strengthening defenses on the northern border to cope with the situation. "Switzerland originally had an air force base near Dubendorf in Zurich, and now plans to disperse the air force concentrated there and move the base to the west to ensure safety." (27th Havas dispatch)

Romania Reduces Oil Exports to Italy

Rome

The quantity of Romanian oil shipped to Italy in February decreased by 80% compared to January. The reason is that when the League of Nations sanctions were implemented, the Romanian government stipulated that all oil shipped to Italy must be paid for in gold coins, but Italy seems unwilling or unable to comply with this. While Romania's oil exports have decreased, its exports of other goods to Italy have also decreased. (26th Reuters dispatch)

Washington

The State Department today released a presidential order transferring St. Thomas Island in the West Indies to the Navy for management in order to establish a permanent naval aviation base. The naval community believes that this plan is very important and is related to fleet maneuvers in the Caribbean Sea and the Pacific Ocean. This island is located 38 miles east of Puerto Rico and is not far from the Panama Canal. St. Thomas Island and other islands were purchased by the United States from Denmark for $25 million in January 1917. (26th Reuters dispatch)

South Manchuria Railway to Be Reorganized by the End of March Setting Up a Central Railway Organization for All of Manchuria Personnel Will Also Be Refreshed at the Same Time

Changchun

In order to cope with the new situation, South Manchuria Railway President Matsuoka has decided to adopt innovative policies for the operation of South Manchuria Railway, including organizational reform and personnel refreshment, and reducing the salaries of subordinates. The plan has been agreed upon by the Kwantung Army and will be resolutely implemented by the end of March.

"Organizational reform" will organically link and control the South Manchuria Railway Department, Construction Bureau, North Korea Railway Administration, and Railway General Bureau, set up a central hub for the operation of "all" Manchuria railways in Shenyang, and conduct various economic investigations and plans.

"Personnel refreshment and salary reduction for subordinates" will resolutely eliminate senior redundant personnel, and make the operation mechanism more rational, and start economic development in the hinterland of North Manchuria, and reduce the salaries of subordinates. U.S. Farmers Loan Bill Vetoed by President

Washington

President Roosevelt today vetoed the $50 million farmers loan bill. The bill stipulates that farmers who cultivate land in accordance with the principles of soil conservation set by the government this year can borrow money from the government. The president stated that the government will use unspent relief funds to make similar loans. As for the reason for his veto, it is because the bill did not determine the method of raising funds. However, the president's veto is not related to the agricultural bill proposed by the government, which still requires approval from a joint session of the House and Senate. (26th National News Agency dispatch)

France to Build New Ship to Develop South American Shipping Industry Costing 180 Million Francs Requires Two and a Half Years to Complete

Paris

Costing 180 Million Francs Requires Two and a Half Years to Complete

Paris

The Minister of Shipping today signed an order to build a new ship to replace the Atlantique (42,512 tons), which was completely destroyed by fire in the English Channel in January 1933. The new ship will still be named Atlantique and will have a displacement of 30,000 tons, dedicated to the shipping industry between the French port of Bordeaux and South America. The ship will cost 180 million francs, employ 4,000 workers, and take two and a half years to build. (26th Reuters dispatch)

Ships at Dagu Port Still Not Out of Danger 37 Ships Trapped Inside and Outside the Port

Tianjin Communication: The Dagu Port has frozen twice, the shipping route is interrupted, and the Chinese and foreign shipping industries are very concerned that the ships trapped outside the port are running out of coal, water, and food, and the crew and passengers are in danger. For days, they have been running between the Haihe Engineering Bureau, the Ministry of Communications Maritime Administration, and the Tianjin Customs Port Affairs Office, pleading for immediate rescue. The responsibility of the three agencies is the greatest for the Haihe Engineering Bureau, so the voices of criticism are also more numerous. On the 22nd, the bureau, unable to resist the supervision, leased the Japanese icebreaker Dalian Maru to sail outside the port to break the ice. However, since the 21st, the weather has been cold and snowy, and the ice has frozen even more firmly. Also, because the northeast wind is very strong, the ice along the Bohai Bay has all accumulated near the Heigu Lighthouse. The Dalian Maru has always been boasted as a newly built large icebreaker, but as a result of the collision, it worked for 27 hours on the 22nd, only advancing seven nautical miles inward from outside the port, still more than ten nautical miles away from the distressed passenger and cargo ships. On the 23rd, the cold exceeded severe winter, and the Dalian Maru was trapped midway due to the thick ice, two nautical miles away from the Japanese ship Shengjing Maru, which was also trapped outside the port. The Tianjin shipping industry believes that the trapped ships (currently 26 trapped outside the port, 11 inside the port) are not only lacking coal, water, and food, but also the hulls of most of the ships have been damaged by the ice, and the goods on board have suffered considerable damage, totaling more than 1.5 million yuan in January. If rescue is not carried out quickly, the losses will be even more immeasurable. That day, an emergency meeting was held, and it was decided to send Wang Gengsan, manager of the Tianjin Shipping Company, and Executive Committee member Dong Haoyun, to visit the Haihe Engineering Bureau, Tianjin Customs, and Tianjin Maritime Administration, requesting to lease the Japanese icebreaker Fengtian Maru and the British icebreaker Mara to assist in the collision. At the same time, the Haihe Engineering Bureau's icebreaker Qingling and Moling also collided outward from Tanggu, working both inside and outside, so that the shipping route could be opened. Although the three agencies have permitted it, the wind direction outside the port changed from northeast to northwest on the morning of the 24th, and the solid ice gradually loosened, so the idea of leasing more icebreakers was abandoned. Unexpectedly, the northwest wind suddenly stopped in the afternoon, and the ice accumulated as before, and the hope of the distressed ships escaping was lost again. The Tianjin shipping industry then sent representatives to visit Pan Yaoxiang, director of the Maritime Administration. Pan said that the only emergency for the ice-trapped ships was to replenish coal and food. However, because the ships could not sail outside the port, the only option was to use airplanes to deliver them. However, there were no airplanes available in North China, so he directly telegraphed the Ministry of Communications, requesting to allocate a Eurasia Aviation Corporation plane to undertake this work, and the cost would be shared by the shipping companies. It was estimated that the plane could come to Tianjin on the 25th, but it failed to arrive that day. At the same time, the shipping industry here received a telegram from outside Dagu Port that the northwest wind had returned, and the weather in Tianjin had also warmed up, and there was hope that the ice would break up. The companies then agreed with the Tianjin Shipping Company to have Wang Gengsan, the manager of the company, take the Tianxing icebreaker, carrying a large amount of coal and food, to sail outside the port in the morning to provide assistance to the distressed ships. The Japanese icebreaker Dalian Maru trapped outside the port and the two icebreakers of the Haihe Engineering Bureau in Tanggu inside the port also sailed outside the port to break the ice after the Tianxing Wheel. According to the observation of the shipping industry, if the weather does not change on the 26th, the ice should flow, and the trapped ships can also move slightly. In another two or three days, they can completely escape. As for the Ministry of Communications' decision to send a Eurasia airplane to provide coal and water to the trapped ships, it replied to the Tianjin Maritime Administration on the 25th, agreeing to send a plane north on the morning of the 27th to land at the Tianjin Dongjuzi Airport, load food, and fly to the outside of the port to deliver it. Pan Yaoxiang, director of the Tianjin Maritime Administration, noted in the Ministry of Communications' telegram that the hourly rental fee for Eurasia planes was 800 yuan. Now, to rescue the trapped ships, which is a charitable act, the gasoline fee will be reduced by 200 yuan per hour. After contacting Xiao Zhenying, the mayor of Tianjin, Xiao agreed to fully donate and bear the gasoline fee of the plane, and sent Liu Dongxuan, director of the Social Affairs Bureau, to cooperate with Pan Yaoxiang, section chief Yang of the Maritime Administration, and the chief of general affairs to take care of the loading of food at the Dongjuzi Airport on the morning of the 26th. The Tianjin shipping industry had already prepared a large amount of food, bread, canned goods, etc. on the 25th, to be loaded at that time. The Maritime Administration also stipulated that the plane's work on the 27th would be divided into three parts:

1. Contact the ships for food.

2. Measure the positions of the trapped ships and investigate the thickness of the ice.

3. Fly to Qinhuangdao to provide food to the ships trapped there. (25th)

Shaanxi Bandits Flee to Shanxi Large Army Prepares to Encircle and Suppress Zhu Shouguang Reports on Bandit Situation Not Difficult to Completely Suppress in a Short Time

Taiyuan Communication: The northern Shaanxi Communists have long had plans to flee to Shanxi, but because the bandits are divided internally and the troops stationed along the river are strictly guarded, the area was able to pass the winter defense last year peacefully. However, according to official reports, suddenly 5,000 to 6,000 Communists crossed the river in the direction of Shilou, and bandit crowds also secretly crossed in the counties of Yongjin and Jixian in southern Shanxi. Officials held emergency meetings on the 23rd and 24th to discuss countermeasures and ordered the armies to encircle and suppress them strictly. As for the situation of the bandits, Chief of Staff Zhu Shenmou of the Sui Appeasement Office reported on the memorial week on the morning of the 24th as follows: "According to a telegram from Division Commander Yang of Fenyang (17th), 200 bandits were also found in the Baoshanshan Mountain behind the Hejiapan on the opposite bank of the Heyu Temple, southwest of Huojiacun in Shilou. Also, at 5:00 PM on the 17th, more than 100 bandits were also found on the east river beach of Sheyu Village on the opposite bank of Niujuan Kou, north of Huojiacun, all crossing eastward on boats. Our artillery fired fiercely one after another, and many bandit boats were destroyed. Only a small number of bandits landed and fled to the mountains. Unexpectedly, at 8:00 PM on the 20th, suddenly 70 to 80 bandits forcibly crossed the east bank in Ping Shang Village, Zhongyang, and more than 100 Communists also crossed in places such as Zhuanjiao and Hejiawa in Shilou. By the morning of Ma (21st), thousands of people had crossed in various directions. Although the river bank defense troops resisted desperately, the number of bandits was too large and could not be contained. On Ma (21st), thousands of people continued to cross, advancing in the three directions of Shilou, Zhongyang, and Lishi. Now, the county town of Shilou has been surrounded. In summary, the number of bandit troops who have crossed the river before and after has reached 5,000 to 6,000, and they are fighting against the troops stationed in Zhongyang, Shilou, and Lishi. Once the headquarters determines the intentions of the bandit troops, it will use the most superior force and the fastest weapons to annihilate them in one fell swoop. It is thought that the bandit troops are isolated and deep, and they have no organized masses, and they are extremely lacking in guns and bullets, and it is not difficult to completely suppress them all in a short time." (24th)

朱淼假造　褚民誼藨函　諉稱因同鄉人請託而發

Zhu Miao Forged a Letter of Recommendation from Chu Minyi, Claiming It Was Issued at the Request of a Fellow Townsman

住居公共租界密勒路興業里第二十八號門牌之浙江溫州人朱淼、卽朱平海、今年二十八歲、於日前私用偽造前行政院秘書長褚民誼之圖章、混發謀職薦信、事為褚民誼得悉、於二十五日將情致函法警務處、請為查究、爰於二十六日由法捕房包探、查得朱匿居蒲柏路大華公寓第二十六號房間內、當往將朱拘獲、並將密勒路興業里寓所搜查、毫無證物、故於昨日下午將朱解送第二特院刑一庭、先由捕房律師姚肇第稱、本案被吿冒用他人之圖章、濫發荐函後、曾被褚民誼之舊屬戴春風發覺、報吿褚氏、轉報法捕房、將被吿拘獲、現以刑法第二一〇二一六·二一七條偽造文書偽造印章等罪起訴、惟案尙未偵查完畢、請求改期、詰之朱淼供稱、前有同鄉人金姓來滬、與我會面、談及他近來失業、他就問我你與褚民誼相熟吾、緣民人前在行政院辦過事的、其實民人與褚民誼不相識、當因友誼情面關係、故民人諉稱相熟的、至此金卽託我轉懇褚民誼、寫一荐函、至甘肅財政廳長處謀荐職位、民人允諾後、卽假造一信、冒蓋褚民誼之圖章、給與金姓、不料金姓竟得此假信、給與褚民誼之舊屬戴春風閱看、以致察破、轉報褚民誼、向捕房吿發、祗此一决、所有偽圖章、已被民人擲入興業里弄口之垃圾桶內是實、王庭長諭朱還押、改期三月四日再核、

Zhu Miao, also known as Zhu Pinghai, a 28-year-old resident of No. 28, Xingye Lane, Miller Road, in the International Settlement, privately forged the seal of Chu Minyi, the former Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, and issued letters of recommendation to seek employment. Chu Minyi learned of this and sent a letter to the French Police Department on the 25th, requesting an investigation. On the 26th, a French detective discovered that Zhu was hiding in Room 26, Dahua Apartments, Bubai Road, and arrested him. A search of his residence in Xingye Lane, Miller Road, yielded no evidence. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, Zhu was sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District. First, the police lawyer, Yao Zhaodi, stated that after the defendant forged and misused another person's seal to issue letters of recommendation, it was discovered by Dai Chunfeng, a former subordinate of Chu Minyi, who reported it to Chu, who then reported it to the French Police Department. The defendant was arrested and is now being prosecuted for the crimes of forging documents and seals under Articles 210, 216, and 217 of the Criminal Law. However, the case has not yet been fully investigated, and a postponement is requested. When questioned, Zhu Miao confessed that a fellow townsman surnamed Jin came to Shanghai, met with him, and mentioned that he had recently lost his job. Jin asked him if he was familiar with Chu Minyi because Jin had previously worked in the Executive Yuan. In fact, he (Zhu) did not know Chu Minyi, but due to friendship, he falsely claimed to be familiar. Thereupon, Jin asked me to implore Chu Minyi to write a letter of recommendation to the Director of the Gansu Department of Finance to seek a position. After he agreed, he forged a letter, fraudulently affixing Chu Minyi's seal, and gave it to Jin. Unexpectedly, Jin showed this forged letter to Dai Chunfeng, a former subordinate of Chu Minyi, which led to its discovery. Dai reported it to Chu Minyi, who reported it to the police. This is the only instance. All the forged seals have been thrown into the trash can at the entrance of Xingye Lane. Judge Wang ordered Zhu to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing for March 4th.

工部局警務處　吉文斯辭職　因意見不洽求去

Resignation of Mr. Givens of the Shanghai Municipal Police Department Due to Disagreement

大美晚報云、工部局警務處政治科主任吉文斯氏、因意見不洽、已定三月二十日辭職、吉氏近因排擊、一二兩月、曾請假多時、並未說明原因、當請假期內、其職務由勞白森氏代理、勞氏現有繼任之望、按吉氏為愛爾蘭人、於一九零七年加入警務處、近數年因屢有勞績、曾由南京政府授與獎章、吉氏茲定三月二十四日歸程返愛、至其意見不洽之眞相、未經當局宣布、

According to the "Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury," Mr. Givens, head of the Political Division of the Shanghai Municipal Police Department, has resigned effective March 20th due to disagreements. Mr. Givens has recently been under pressure, having taken a long leave of absence in January and February without stating the reason. During his leave, his duties were handled by Mr. Laubeson, who is now expected to succeed him. Mr. Givens is Irish and joined the police department in 1907. In recent years, he has received medals from the Nanjing government for his meritorious service. Mr. Givens is scheduled to return to Ireland on March 24th. The true nature of his disagreement has not been announced by the authorities.

Chen Ruifu, a 30-year-old man from Ningbo, of modest means, employed at the Yingli Import and Export Company at 97 Renji Road, built a residence at 50 Zhende Lane, Huishan Road. Eleven years ago, he married Wang Minghua (31 years old), a woman from the same hometown, and they lived together in the residence. The couple had a very harmonious relationship, but recently, Wang's attitude suddenly changed drastically, and she did not return home on Tuesday and Saturday nights, arousing suspicion that she was having an affair. Wang then tried to investigate and discovered that her husband was cohabitating with Wu Zhenzhi (23 years old), a woman from Hangzhou, at No. 47, Shufeng South Lane, Baoding Road, nearby. Therefore, at 6:15 AM on the 21st of the month, she went to the Huishan Police Station to file a complaint. Detective Huang Fugen and investigator Gu Zhongshu, accompanied by Wang Minghua, went to the address. After knocking on the door for a long time, Chen Ruifu finally opened it, and he was already dressed. They were both taken to the police station for questioning and then released. They then reported to the First Special District Court and obtained a summons. Yesterday morning, Chen Ruifu and Wu Zhenzhi were summoned to the Fifth Criminal Court of the First Special District, where Judge Huang Risheng presided over the trial. The police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, stated the circumstances at the time and prosecuted them for adultery under Article 239 of the Criminal Law. He also stated that the defendant, Chen Ruifu, confessed to the police that he had been cohabitating with Wu Zhenzhi since March of the 23rd year, which is now more than two years. At that time, the plaintiff even went to look for a house and arranged for furniture. Afterwards, on the morning of the 24th, the defendant, Chen Ruifu, reported to the police station that the plaintiff and the servant had left the residence, taking with them 350 shares of the tram company's stock, each share worth 38 yuan, and 50 pieces of silverware. Since the police station had no corroborating evidence, it only allowed him to file a report. However, the plaintiff also reported to the police station that she had moved to Qi's house on Foch Road for fear of harassment by the defendant. Both parties are in court today and should be questioned. Wang Minghua testified that she only learned of the defendant's cohabitation two months ago. The defendants, Chen Ruifu, and others, stated that the plaintiff was aware of this. They presented witnesses Jin Zhenmin (a resident of Shufeng South Lane) to prove that the plaintiff and Chen Ruifu had looked at the house together at the time. Her younger sister, Chen Ruidi, testified that before her brother and Wu Zhenzhi cohabitated, she was entrusted by her brother to notify the plaintiff. An Indian man named Aijieke testified that a year ago, the plaintiff went to the defendant's cohabitation place, intending to open the door and enter, but failed, and then went to my house at No. 45, intending to cross over to No. 47 from the sun deck, but I refused, etc. Wang Minghua denied the words of all the witnesses. Judge Huang, believing that the plaintiff and defendants were a couple of many years, advised them to reconcile to avoid hurting their feelings, but Wang insisted on prosecuting. The police clerk Qian Zashi stated that the evidence presented by the defendant needed to be investigated further and requested more time to allow both parties to reconcile. Judge Huang approved the report and ordered the trial to be adjourned for one week.

Li Bangxiang, a Cantonese tea merchant who lives at 9 Deqing Lane, 9 Muerming Road, has a wife, Lu, who is 34 years old. They have two maidservants at home, the elder named Cunmei, who is 11 years old, and the younger named Laixi, who is 7 years old. However, Li Lu is quite violent and usually abuses the two maidservants in every way, beating them with bamboo poles and shoes, causing them to be injured. Seeing this, people reported it to the Chinese Children's Welfare Association. On December 3rd of last year, the association sent Zhao, a clerk, to report to the Chengdu Road Police Station, ordering Chinese and Western detectives to go to investigate. They saw the maidservant Cunmei with her hands tied behind her back to the bed and sewn together with thread, not allowing her to move. Because Li Lu happened to be out at the time, she was not arrested. The two maidservants were taken back to the police station, transferred to the hospital, and found to have injuries. The next day, they were sent to the First Special Court. They were instructed to keep Cunmei and Laixi temporarily at the Ji Liang Institute and issued a warrant ordering Li to come to the case for questioning. At 6:30 AM yesterday morning, Li Lu, accompanied by her lawyer Ge Zhaosai, turned herself in to the Chengdu Road Police Station and was immediately transferred to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. A public prosecution was filed in accordance with Article 286 of the Criminal Law, charging her with abuse. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated that on December 3rd of last year, Zhao Jian, a clerk from the Chinese Children's Welfare Association, reported to the police station that a woman at 9 Deqing Lane, Muerming Road, was abusing two maidservants. The police station sent detectives to the scene and saw Cunmei tied to the bed. She confessed that she had been abused by her mistress, Li Lu. Therefore, Cunmei and another maidservant, Laixi, were taken to the police station and sent to Guangren Hospital. After examination by the doctor, it was found that Cunmei had injuries on her forehead and right hand, and Laixi had injuries on both arms. In addition to sending the two maidservants to the Ji Liang Institute, because Li Lu's whereabouts were uncertain, and it was rumored that she had gone to Beiping, the court issued a warrant for her arrest. Only this morning did she turn herself in to the police station with her lawyer. Because time was short, there was not enough time to notify the Ji Liang Institute to send the two girls to the case, so he requested a postponement. Subsequently, the defendant's lawyer applied for bail. Judge Wu Zehan ordered that Li Lu be released on bail of 2,000 yuan and adjourned the trial for further questioning.

Securities - Final Delivery of Old Bonds - Unified Government Bonds to Be Delivered Today - Seven Types of New and Old Bonds to Be Auctioned

Yesterday, February 27, at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, was the date for the final delivery of the February futures old bonds. The total number of deliveries was 50,265,000 yuan, including 38,475,000 yuan delivered through the exchange and 11,790,000 yuan transferred between brokers. The receiving side was mostly for arbitrage trading in the financial sector, and the delivering side was also mostly in the financial sector, with a considerable number of retail investors receiving deliveries. The process was turbulent, and the market was extremely shaken. From the beginning of the February futures on December 30 of last year, after more than half a month of market closure, the highest and lowest differences were 16.1 yuan for disarmament, 14.75 yuan for gold short, 13.05 yuan for whole six, and 9.45 yuan for salt tax. The biggest reason for the decline was the long-brewing interest rate reduction issue since the Lunar New Year, which became increasingly serious, and short sellers were very active. Until February 1, the government formally announced the Unified Government Bond measures, and at the same time, due to rumors, the exchange was ordered to suspend trading for more than half a month to strictly investigate whether public officials had engaged in speculative manipulation. The market only reopened on February 17. However, in order to limit speculation and maintain market prices, short sellers were required to submit physical goods, and new selling was prohibited. After a sharp drop in market prices, arbitrage trading in the financial sector slightly increased market prices. The final closing market prices were mostly 68% off for Unified Class A, 66% off for Unified Class B, 63.5% off for Unified Class C, Unified Class D was not related to old bonds, and 62.5% off for Unified Class E. The future prospect is that banks will engage in arbitrage and maintenance, and Unified Government Bonds will be auctioned starting today, and market prices should improve slightly. The order of auctioning Unified Government Bonds will be Unified E, Unified D, Unified C, Unified B, Unified A, Gold Long, and 96, for a total of seven types. During the period for exchanging old bonds for Unified Government Bonds, those who have not yet exchanged for new bonds can use receipts from exchange offices and banks such as Zhong Zhong Jiao for delivery. However, each receipt is limited to a face value of 5,000 yuan to facilitate circulation. The February futures delivery clearing and total transaction volume are listed separately below (unit: 100 yuan).

If any falsification is found, not only will the original goods be confiscated, but there will also be penalties. Shen Bao Literary and Art Weekly Special: The Pure Poet by Leng Mo

Opening any literary history, the first part always discusses poetry. Only poetry has a long history, and throughout this long period, poetry has never declined. Every era has great poets, and poetry seems to have a permanent life. Originally, poetry is the most natural of all literary products and should be as long-lasting as nature. However, this only applies to poetry that is truly a natural product. Artificial encouragement to produce forms and quantities during a certain period has little to do with sustaining the life of poetry. We cannot hope to produce more poets now, nor can we hope that poets will produce more works. Even if we could hope for this and even if this hope could be fulfilled, the result might only be a waste of energy.

Until now, poet still seems to be the most floating title for those engaged in art. Whether novelist, playwright, musician, or painter, when they reach their highest reputation, they are also given the title of poet. Therefore, artists all hope to become poets. Of course, this position does not necessarily have to be obtained by writing poetry, but the desire to directly obtain the title of poet by writing poetry is possessed by at least a portion of people. At least our past literati have given us a good example. Almost every family's collection of writings contains a part of poetry. In

Legislative Yuan Finance Committee Reviews Amendment to Ministry of Finance Organic Law 41

Nanjing. The Legislative Yuan Finance Committee's preliminary review of the draft amendment to the Ministry of Finance Organic Law concluded on the 27th. Four committee members, including Tui Chen Chang-heng, were appointed to organize the articles. The Legal and Financial Committees will jointly review the articles again at a set date. It is heard that the contents include changing the Accounting Division to an Accounting Department, and establishing an Audit Division. The Salt Affairs Bureau and Salt Affairs Audit Office will remain largely unchanged, as the Ministry of Finance advocates maintaining the original organization. (27th, Special Dispatch)

Nanjing. The Regulations on Savings for Civil Servants will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. The regulations stipulate that all civil servants serving in governments at all levels and their subordinate agencies must deposit a fixed rate monthly. Personnel serving in party headquarters at all levels are also regarded as civil servants. Savings will be in the form of fixed deposits with zero deposit payments, handled by the Central Trust Bureau. (27th, Special Dispatch)

Nanjing. The Legislative Yuan’s Legal and Economic Committees jointly reviewed the draft amendment to the organizational regulations of seven agencies under the Ministry of Industry on the morning of the 27th. The result was a resolution that no amendments were necessary and the bill was to be submitted to the plenary session for deliberation on the morning of the 28th. (27th, Central News Agency)

Regulations for Appointment of Police Officers Promulgated 42

Nanjing. The National Government officially promulgated the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Regulations on the Appointment of Police Officers on the 27th. The full text consists of ten articles and will be implemented from the date of promulgation. (27th, Central News Agency)

Ministry of Railways Orders the Dissolution of the Preparatory Office for the Exhibition of Products Along the Railway 43

Nanjing. On the 27th, the Ministry of Railways ordered the dissolution of the Preparatory Office for the Exhibition of Products Along the Railway. Unfinished matters are to be transferred to the Ministry's Business Division for handling on the 29th. The fourth Railway Exhibition, originally scheduled to be held in Xi'an in July of this year, has also been suspended. (27th, Special Dispatch)

Inheritance Tax Should Be Levied After Implementing Income Tax 44

Nanjing. The inheritance tax proposal has been resolved by the Executive Yuan to be submitted for review. According to Jiang Tingfu, there is nothing objectionable in theory regarding levying inheritance tax. However, it should be done after implementing income tax, otherwise, it will be difficult to implement. The method of collecting income tax in our country was approved by the Executive Yuan two years ago and submitted to the Central Political Conference. However, it has been shelved for two years and has not yet been resolved. Currently, the implementation of inheritance tax can only be carried out after this matter is decided. (27th, Central News Agency)

Ministry of Finance Stipulates Measures for Exporting Industrial Salt to Japan 45

Nanjing. According to the Sino-Japanese agreement, industrial salt exported from China to Japan should be supplied by Qingdao. The export must be handled by designated industrial salt exporters. However, the salt production in the Changlu and Huaibei areas is excessive. Merchants from Lu and Huai have repeatedly petitioned the Ministry of Finance, requesting permission to export salt to Japan. In order to maintain the livelihood of Qingdao salt producers, the Ministry has specially stipulated three measures: 1. If Lu, Huai, and other producing areas have surplus salt for export to Japan for industrial use, and Japanese merchants place orders with companies in those areas, they must obtain certification from the Japanese Monopoly Bureau according to the current Qingdao regulations before they can export the salt to Japan. 2. Qingdao salt should be given priority for shipment to Japan. If Qingdao still has salt in storage, and other areas request to export salt, the tax rate for those areas should be two dimes per market dan, according to the export regulations for Chinese salt. 3. Other procedures for transporting salt to Japan should generally follow the export regulations for Chinese salt. (27th, Central News Agency)

Ministry of Finance Informs Provinces and Cities to Pay Attention to the Issuance of Gift Certificates by Stores 46

Nanjing. The Ministry of Finance believes that the issuance of gift certificates by banks and companies is originally intended to facilitate social interactions. If the styles and patterns do not resemble banknotes, they are naturally not subject to prohibition. Gift certificates issued by ordinary stores, such as candle coupons and noodle coupons, are also intended to facilitate social interactions. However, they can harm the people if the store closes down. The Ministry has now informed the provincial and municipal governments that the competent authorities should pay attention to the issuance of various gift certificates at all times to prevent abuses. (27th, Central News Agency)
